The mango genome is highly heterozygous and also experienced a recent WGD event, rendering substantial challenges for mango genome assembly [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 44" title="Veeckman E, Ruttink T, Vandepoele K. Are we there yet? Reliably estimating the completeness of plant genome sequences. Plant Cell. 2016;28:175968." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR44" id="ref-link-section-d6606e1775">44</a>]. Sequencing technologies producing long reads have facilitated the recent assembly of highly heterozygous genomes, such as those of durian [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 45" title="Teh BT, Lim K, Yong CH, Ng CCY, Rao SR, Rajasegaran V, Lim WK, Ong CK, Chan K, Cheng VKY, et al. The draft genome of tropical fruit durian (Durio zibethinus). Nat Genet. 2017;49:163341." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR45" id="ref-link-section-d6606e1778">45</a>], oak [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 46" title="Plomion C, Aury JM, Amselem J, Leroy T, Murat F, Duplessis S, Faye S, Francillonne N, Labadie K, Le Provost G, et al. Oak genome reveals facets of long lifespan. Nat Plants. 2018;4:44052." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR46" id="ref-link-section-d6606e1781">46</a>], and <i>Gnetum montanum</i> [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 47" title="Wan T, Liu ZM, Li LF, Leitch AR, Leitch IJ, Lohaus R, Liu ZJ, Xin HP, Gong YB, Liu Y, et al. A genome for gnetophytes and early evolution of seed plants. Nat Plants. 2018;4:829." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR47" id="ref-link-section-d6606e1787">47</a>]. We addressed the issues of high heterozygosity and WGD primarily by using long (PacBio) reads, in association with NGS sequencing, Hi-C mapping, and a high-density integrated linkage map, through which we have produced a chromosome-level genome assembly for mango (<i>Mangifera indica</i>). To our knowledge, this is the first and most complete genome assembly of mango. The genome assembly provides a useful resource for mango breeding and also is valuable for understanding the biochemistry and evolution of specialized metabolism for urushiols and related phenols in Anacardiaceae.</p><p>WGD events, or polyploidization, occurred throughout the routes of plant evolution, which are important drivers for specialization and emergence of novel traits and functions [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Wolfe KH. Yesterdays polyploids and the mystery of diploidization. Nat Rev Genet. 2001;2:33341." href="#ref-CR48" id="ref-link-section-d6606e1797">48</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Jiao Y, Wickett NJ, Ayyampalayam S, Chanderbali AS, Landherr L, Ralph PE, Tomsho LP, Hu Y, Liang H, Soltis PS, et al. Ancestral polyploidy in seed plants and angiosperms. Nature. 2011;473:97100." href="#ref-CR49" id="ref-link-section-d6606e1797_1">49</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Blanc G, Wolfe KH. Widespread paleopolyploidy in model plant species inferred from age distributions of duplicate genes. Plant Cell. 2004;16:166778." href="#ref-CR50" id="ref-link-section-d6606e1797_2">50</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 51" title="Vanneste K, Baele G, Maere S, Van de Peer Y. Analysis of 41 plant genomes supports a wave of successful genome duplications in association with the Cretaceous-Paleogene boundary. Genome Res. 2014;24:133447." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR51" id="ref-link-section-d6606e1800">51</a>]. Consequences of WGD offer genetic preconditions for successful domestication which is responsible for the advent of many crops [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 52" title="Salman-Minkov A, Sabath N, Mayrose I. Whole-genome duplication as a key factor in crop domestication. Nat Plants. 2016;2:16115." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR52" id="ref-link-section-d6606e1803">52</a>]. The recent WGD in mango genome (~33MYA) occurred long after the split of Anacardiaceae from Rutaceae and Sapindaceae (~70MYA based on our results) and even after the advent of the family Anacardiaceae (54.874.9MYA) [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 53" title="Alexandra N, Muellner-Rieh AW, Joshua W, Clayton SB, Nauheimer L, SCSKP Y-CC. Molecular phylogenetics and molecular clock dating of Sapindales based on plastid rbcL, atpB and trnL-trnF DN. 2016;65." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR53" id="ref-link-section-d6606e1806">53</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 54" title="Muellner AN, Vassiliades DD, Renner SS. Placing Biebersteiniaceae, a herbaceous clade of Sapindales, in a temporal and geographic context. Pl Syst Evol. 2007;266:20." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR54" id="ref-link-section-d6606e1809">54</a>]. Mango belongs to the genus <i>Mangifera</i> which can be classified under the tribe Anacardieae. Despite the availability of molecular systematics data of Anacardiaceae [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 55" title="Pell SK: Molecular systematics of the cashew family (Anacardiaceae). PhD Thesis 2004:193." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR55" id="ref-link-section-d6606e1816">55</a>], a detailed molecular clock dating of the species within the family is lacking, and no other chromosome-level Anacardiaceae genome is currently available [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 56" title="Zeng L, Tu XL, Dai H, Han FM, Lu BS, Wang MS, Nanaei HA, Tajabadipour A, Mansouri M, Li XL, et al. Whole genomes and transcriptomes reveal adaptation and domestication of pistachio. Genome Biol. 2019;20:79." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR56" id="ref-link-section-d6606e1819">56</a>], which hamper our detailed estimation of WGD event time. However, we observed preferential post-WGD retaining of duplicated genes involved in energy metabolism, such as photosynthesis and lipid biosynthesis. Considering that the recent WGD event occurred within the period of drastic decline of atmospheric carbon dioxide concentrations resulting in a descent into icehouse climate [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 57" title="Pearson PN, Palmer MR. Atmospheric carbon dioxide concentrations over the past 60 million years. Nature. 2000;406:6959." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR57" id="ref-link-section-d6606e1822">57</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 58" title="Grein M, Konrad W, Wilde V, Utescher T, Roth-Nebelsick A. Reconstruction of atmospheric CO2 during the early middle Eocene by application of a gas exchange model to fossil plants from the Messel Formation, Germany. Palaeogeogr Palaeoclimatol Palaeoecol. 2011;309:9." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR58" id="ref-link-section-d6606e1825">58</a>], it is appealing to hypothesize that the preferential retaining of the duplicated energy metabolism genes is the result of adaptive evolution to cope with the decline of carbon dioxide as an essential substrate for carbon fixation and shrinking capability of the plant photosynthesis and energy assimilation by icehouse climate.</p><p>Urushiols and related phenols (e.g., anacardic acids) are produced in many Anacardiaceae plants, with a 15- or 17-carbon side chain that is responsible for allergic skin rash [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 36" title="Dunn IS, Liberato DJ, Castagnoli N Jr, Byers VS. Influence of chemical reactivity of urushiol-type haptens on sensitization and the induction of tolerance. Cell Immunol. 1986;97:18996." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR36" id="ref-link-section-d6606e1831">36</a>]. These phenols are likely defensive molecules against fungi, insects, and herbivorous vertebrates [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Miriam Cojocaru SD, Glotter E, Goldman A, Gottlieb HE, Jacoby B, Prusky D. 5-(12-Heptadecenyl)-resorcinol, the major component of the antifungal activity in the peel of mango fruit. Phytochemistry. 1986;25:3." href="#ref-CR59" id="ref-link-section-d6606e1834">59</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Greg I Johnson MAaPL: Resin ducts in the mango fruit: a defence system. J Exp Bot 1980, 31:2." href="#ref-CR60" id="ref-link-section-d6606e1834_1">60</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 61" title="Brian D. escalation of plant defense: do latex and resin canals spur plant diversification? Am Nat. 1991;138:20." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR61" id="ref-link-section-d6606e1837">61</a>]. Nevertheless, they have the potential for the treatment of cancer and skin and viral diseases [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 62" title="Edwards EK. Spontaneous repigmentation of vitiligo following generalized acute allergic contact dermatitis. Contact Dermatitis. 1995;33." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR62" id="ref-link-section-d6606e1840">62</a>]. Phenolic compounds are diverse, and the diversification of phenols is based on the general phenolic biosynthesis pathway, in which early genes like chaconne synthase (CHS) have important contributions to the metabolic flow of phenols in plants [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 31" title="Abe I, Morita H. Structure and function of the chalcone synthase superfamily of plant type III polyketide synthases. Nat Prod Rep. 2010;27:80938." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR31" id="ref-link-section-d6606e1843">31</a>]. Extensive expansion of CHS genes in the mango genome highlights the important roles of CHS in mango. The expansion before the recent WGD but after the split of Anacardiaceae and ancestor of Rutaceae and Sapindaceae indicates the <i>CHS</i> genes might have been expanded in the early stages of Anacardiaceae emergence. Our results show that extensive duplications lead to a large number of members in clade III of <i>CHS</i> genes, and, for the highly expressed genes, they tend to be highly expressed in barks and peels rather than in the flesh of all the four varieties we investigated; this is comparable to high accumulation of urushiols in these tissues in mangoes, suggesting their important roles in the biosynthesis of urushiols in mangoes [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2" title="Schulze-Kaysers N, Feuereisen MM, Schieber A. Phenolic compounds in edible species of the anacardiaceae family - a review. RSC Adv. 2015;5:14." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR2" id="ref-link-section-d6606e1853">2</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 63" title="Nott PE, Roberts C. A synthesis of mangiferin. Phytochemistry. 1967;6:3." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR63" id="ref-link-section-d6606e1856">63</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 64" title="Ansari MAE, Reddy KK, Sastry KNS, Nayudamma Y. Polyphenols of Mangifera indica. Phytochemistry. 1971;10:3." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR64" id="ref-link-section-d6606e1859">64</a>]. As urushiols are specific to and commonly accumulated in Anacardiaceae to varying levels, it will be interesting to investigate if <i>CHS</i> genes follow similar patterns of gene family evolution in other species when more Anacardiaceae genomes are available which might help understand the mechanisms and evolution of the family-specific phenol biosynthesis.</p><p>It is widely accepted that there are two centers of domestication: one in India, a majority of which are monoembryoonic, and the other in continental Southeast Asia, most of which are polyembryonic [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 42" title="Schnell RJ, Olano CT, Meerow AW, Campbell RJ, Kuhm DN. Mango genetic diversity analysis and pedigree inferences for Florida cultivars using microsatellite. J AMER Soc HORT SCI. 2006;13:11." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR42" id="ref-link-section-d6606e1868">42</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 43" title="RJ. BJaS: The mango: botany, production and uses. In The mango: botany, production and uses. Edited by RE L. Wallingford: CAB International; 1997: 27." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR43" id="ref-link-section-d6606e1871">43</a>]. Mango cultivars in Florida, USA, are unique, as they have a long history of breeding, and many of the cultivars are descendants of Mulgoba, the only one survived among the six grafted mangoes introduced from India in the late nineteenth century [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 8" title="Knight RJ Jr, Schnell RJ. Mango introduction in Florida and the Haden cultivars significance to the modern industry. Econ Bot. 1994;48:7." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR8" id="ref-link-section-d6606e1874">8</a>]. During the past decades, Chinese breeders have successfully bred several varieties which demonstrate superior performance. With the availability of high-quality reference genome and resequencing data, we have an unprecedented opportunity to closely study genetic components and compare mango germplasms with different backgrounds. This can help clarify relationships of many mango varieties, on which efforts have been made by other approaches [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 8" title="Knight RJ Jr, Schnell RJ. Mango introduction in Florida and the Haden cultivars significance to the modern industry. Econ Bot. 1994;48:7." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR8" id="ref-link-section-d6606e1877">8</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 42" title="Schnell RJ, Olano CT, Meerow AW, Campbell RJ, Kuhm DN. Mango genetic diversity analysis and pedigree inferences for Florida cultivars using microsatellite. J AMER Soc HORT SCI. 2006;13:11." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR42" id="ref-link-section-d6606e1880">42</a>]. Our results show that the mango varieties can be clustered into two groups, coinciding with the proposed two centers of domestication, and allelic admixture was observed in the genomes of commercial varieties.</p><p>Although grouping with Southeast Asia germplasms, landraces indigenous in China forming distinct clades and some have clear allelic admixture. These represent unique genetic resources for future mango breeding endeavors. Landraces have long been recognized as a source of traits for improving yield, nutrition, and abiotic stress adaptation. They are especially important as agricultural production is affected by worldwide climate change [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 65" title="Dwivedi SL, Ceccarelli S, Blair MW, Upadhyaya HD, Are AK, Ortiz R. Landrace germplasm for improving yield and abiotic stress adaptation. Trends Plant Sci. 2016;21:3142." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR65" id="ref-link-section-d6606e1887">65</a>]. Varieties widely cultivated are facing common issues such as alternate bearing, narrow ripening window, poor fruit quality, and cold sensitivity [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2" title="Schulze-Kaysers N, Feuereisen MM, Schieber A. Phenolic compounds in edible species of the anacardiaceae family - a review. RSC Adv. 2015;5:14." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR2" id="ref-link-section-d6606e1890">2</a>]. It is essential to broaden the repository of genetic resources by exploring more exotic germplasms. The landraces in South China represent a valuable resource for future breeding. However, the agronomic and quality characters of these landraces are currently poorly understood, and the genetic resources are threatened by modern agricultural practices and expansion of industries. It is urgent to proceed with comprehensive studies on these landraces. We believe these landraces might not be only germplasms distinct from the mainstream varieties. The availability of the mango genome lays the ground for a more thorough survey of landraces, which would be critical for the improvement of agronomic and quality traits of current mango varieties.</p></div></div></section><section aria-labelledby="Sec10" data-title="Conclusions"><div class="c-article-section" id="Sec10-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Sec10">Conclusions</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Sec10-content"><p>We have generated a mango genome assembly, which is, to our knowledge, the first publically available genome resource for mangoes. This provides crucial information for the study of the evolution of not only mangoes, but the Anacardiaceae family. And this will facilitate the establishment of genome-enabled breeding programs for mango. We estimated that the mango genome underwent an event of whole-genome duplication (WGD) about 33 million years ago. Interestingly, duplicated genes involved in photosynthesis and lipid metabolism are preferentially retained in the mango genome, which likely provides adaptive advantages to sharp historical decreases of concentrations of atmospheric carbon dioxide. Sixty-eight percent of gene families were expanded in the mango genome; among them, genes of <i>chalcone synthase</i> (<i>CHS</i>) were extensively duplicated, which are mostly results of tandem duplications prior to WGD. Particular <i>CHS</i> genes showed universally higher expression in peels among mango varieties, which are likely involved in the biosynthesis of urushiols and related phenols, a group of Anacardiaceae-specific phenols which can induce contact dermatitis. Two distinct groups of mango varieties through genome resequencing, with commercial varieties clustered with India germplasms, which demonstrate allelic admixture. Although grouped with Southeast Asia germplasms, landraces indigenous in South China formed distinct clades, some of which showed admixture.</p></div></div></section><section aria-labelledby="Sec11" data-title="Methods"><div class="c-article-section" id="Sec11-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Sec11">Methods</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Sec11-content"><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec12">Genome survey sequencing</h3><p>Genome survey sequencing was firstly carried out to identify mango accessions suited for whole-genome sequencing. Twenty-two mango cultivar/landrace samplings from the Chinese Academy of Agricultural Sciences Tropical Resources Institute of tropical crop varieties (Hainan, China) were sequenced with Hiseq2000 at about 20 genomic coverage. Leaf genomic DNA isolation, paired-end library construction, and sequencing were carried out as described in our previous publication [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 66" title="Tang C, Yang M, Fang Y, Luo Y, Gao S, Xiao X, An Z, Zhou B, Zhang B, Tan X, et al. The rubber tree genome reveals new insights into rubber production and species adaptation. Nat Plants. 2016;2:16073." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR66" id="ref-link-section-d6606e1922">66</a>]. Genome size, heterozygosity, and repeat content were estimated with a <i>k</i>-mer method using Jellyfish (v2.1.3) [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 67" title="Marcais G, Kingsford C. A fast, lock-free approach for efficient parallel counting of occurrences of k-mers. Bioinformatics. 2011;27:76470." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR67" id="ref-link-section-d6606e1928">67</a>]. Of the 22 sequenced mango cultivars/landraces, Alphonso has a relatively smaller genome size, lower heterozygosity rate, and repeat content. Considering that Alphonso has a clear breeding history and was used as primary breeding germplasm, we chose it as the material for the whole-genome short-gun sequencing using a single molecular sequencing strategy. Meanwhile, GenomeScope [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 68" title="Vurture GW, Sedlazeck FJ, Nattestad M, Underwood CJ, Fang H, Gurtowski J, Schatz MC. GenomeScope: fast reference-free genome profiling from short reads. Bioinformatics. 2017;33:22024." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR68" id="ref-link-section-d6606e1931">68</a>] and ALLPATHS-LG (v52488) [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 69" title="Gnerre S, Maccallum I, Przybylski D, Ribeiro FJ, Burton JN, Walker BJ, Sharpe T, Hall G, Shea TP, Sykes S, et al. High-quality draft assemblies of mammalian genomes from massively parallel sequence data. Proc Natl Acad Sci U S A. 2011;108:15138." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR69" id="ref-link-section-d6606e1934">69</a>] were also used to investigate the genome profile of Alphonso cultivar. The estimated genome size of Alphonso cultivar is ~360Mb, and the estimated heterozygosity rate is ~1.5%. The raw reads of genome survey sequencing are deposited in the NCBI Sequence Read Archive under project ID PRJNA487154 [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 70" title="Wang P, Luo YF, Jianfeng Huang, Shenghan Gao, Guopeng Zhu, Zhiguo Dang, Jiangtao Gai, Meng Yang, Min Zhu, Huangkai Zhang, Xiuxu Ye, Aiping Gao, Xinyu Tan, Sen Wang, Shuangyang Wu, Edgar B. Cahoon, Beibei Bai, Zhichang Zhao, Qian Li, Junya Wei, Huarui Chen, Ruixiong Luo, Deyong Gong, Kexuan Tang, Bing Zhang, Zhangguang Ni, Guodi Huang, Songnian Hu, Yeyuan Chen: Mango (Mangifera indica) Genome sequencing, assembly, resequencing and RNA sequencing. NCBI Sequence Read Archive, &#xA;https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/bioproject/PRJNA487154&#xA;&#xA; (2020)." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR70" id="ref-link-section-d6606e1938">70</a>]. For additional information, see Additionalfile<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#MOESM1">1</a>: Supplementary Notes.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec13">Transcriptome data production and analysis</h3><p>Total RNA was extracted from mango tissues using TRIzol. Subsequent mRNA extraction and mRNA-seq libraries were conducted using Kapa transcriptome kits and sequenced with Hiseq3000. Qualified reads ware mapped to mango assembly guided by gene annotation models using hisat2 (v2.0.4), and the expression level for each gene was performed by Stringtie (v 1.2.3) [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 71" title="Pertea M, Kim D, Pertea GM, Leek JT, Salzberg SL. Transcript-level expression analysis of RNA-seq experiments with HISAT, StringTie and Ballgown. Nat Protoc. 2016;11:165067." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR71" id="ref-link-section-d6606e1952">71</a>]. Pearson correlation coefficient for each gene pair was calculated with custom PERL scripts. The raw data of transcriptomic sequencing are deposited in the NCBI Sequence Read Archive under project ID PRJNA487154 [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 70" title="Wang P, Luo YF, Jianfeng Huang, Shenghan Gao, Guopeng Zhu, Zhiguo Dang, Jiangtao Gai, Meng Yang, Min Zhu, Huangkai Zhang, Xiuxu Ye, Aiping Gao, Xinyu Tan, Sen Wang, Shuangyang Wu, Edgar B. Cahoon, Beibei Bai, Zhichang Zhao, Qian Li, Junya Wei, Huarui Chen, Ruixiong Luo, Deyong Gong, Kexuan Tang, Bing Zhang, Zhangguang Ni, Guodi Huang, Songnian Hu, Yeyuan Chen: Mango (Mangifera indica) Genome sequencing, assembly, resequencing and RNA sequencing. NCBI Sequence Read Archive, &#xA;https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/bioproject/PRJNA487154&#xA;&#xA; (2020)." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR70" id="ref-link-section-d6606e1955">70</a>].</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec14">Genome sequencing and assembly</h3><p>The single-molecule long reads were generated from 1 cell run on the PacBio Sequel II Platform. A total of 86.5-Gb long reads (~240 based on estimated 36) were generated and de novo assembled using CANU (version 1.8) [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 72" title="Koren S, Walenz BP, Berlin K, Miller JR, Bergman NH, Phillippy AM. CANU: scalable and accurate long-read assembly via adaptive k-mer weighting and repeat separation. Genome Res. 2017;27:72236." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR72" id="ref-link-section-d6606e1966">72</a>]. The pair-end and mate-pair short reads were generated by HiSeq2000 and MiSeq platform, including 2 TruSeq PCR-free pair-end libraries with an insert size of 180bp and 500bp and 4 Nextera mate-pair libraries with an insert size of 3kb, 5kb, 8kb, and 10kb. The short reads were also independently assembled by ALLPATHS-LG (v52488) [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 69" title="Gnerre S, Maccallum I, Przybylski D, Ribeiro FJ, Burton JN, Walker BJ, Sharpe T, Hall G, Shea TP, Sykes S, et al. High-quality draft assemblies of mammalian genomes from massively parallel sequence data. Proc Natl Acad Sci U S A. 2011;108:15138." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR69" id="ref-link-section-d6606e1969">69</a>] to investigate the genome profile including estimated genome size and SNP rate for cross-checking. The initial Canu assembly was corrected using a combination of long and short reads with Pilon (v1.23) [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 73" title="Walker BJ, Abeel T, Shea T, Priest M, Abouelliel A, Sakthikumar S, Cuomo CA, Zeng Q, Wortman J, Young SK, Earl AM. Pilon: an integrated tool for comprehensive microbial variant detection and genome assembly improvement. PLoS One. 2014;9:e112963." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR73" id="ref-link-section-d6606e1972">73</a>]. Duplicated assembled haploid contigs were purged using PurgeHaplotigs [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 74" title="Roach MJ, Schmidt SA, Borneman AR. Purge Haplotigs: allelic contig reassignment for third-gen diploid genome assemblies. BMC Bioinformatics. 2018;19:460." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR74" id="ref-link-section-d6606e1975">74</a>], which reduced the assembly from 624.85 to 363.08Mb. A Hi-C library was constructed and sequenced on the Illumina NovaSeq platform for chromosome-level scaffolding. With the Hi-C library, the purged contigs were anchored into super-scaffolds using Juicer [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 75" title="Durand NC, Shamim MS, Machol I, Rao SS, Huntley MH, Lander ES, Aiden EL. Juicer provides a one-click system for analyzing loop-resolution Hi-C experiments. Cell Syst. 2016;3:958." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR75" id="ref-link-section-d6606e1978">75</a>] and 3d-dna pipeline [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 76" title="Dudchenko O, Batra SS, Omer AD, Nyquist SK, Hoeger M, Durand NC, Shamim MS, Machol I, Lander ES, Aiden AP, Aiden EL. De novo assembly of the Aedes aegypti genome using Hi-C yields chromosome-length scaffolds. Science. 2017;356:925." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR76" id="ref-link-section-d6606e1982">76</a>]. ALLMAPS (version 1.0) [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 77" title="Tang H, Zhang X, Miao C, Zhang J, Ming R, Schnable JC, Schnable PS, Lyons E, Lu J. ALLMAPS: robust scaffold ordering based on multiple maps. Genome Biol. 2015;16:3." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR77" id="ref-link-section-d6606e1985">77</a>] was used to anchor the Hi-C super-scaffolds with unique mapped genetic markers from the previous published mango genetic map [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 78" title="Deshpande AB, Anamika K, Jha V, Chidley HG, Oak PS, Kadoo NY, Pujari KH, Giri AP, Gupta VS. Transcriptional transitions in Alphonso mango (Mangifera indica L.) during fruit development and ripening explain its distinct aroma and shelf life characteristics. Sci Rep. 2017;7:8711." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR78" id="ref-link-section-d6606e1988">78</a>]. Finally, the genome assembly contains 20 pseudochromosomal molecules, 2 organelles, and 230 unplaced scaffolds. The raw data of genome deep sequencing (second and third generation sequencing) together with genome assembly are deposited in the NCBI Sequence Read Archive under project ID PRJNA487154 [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 70" title="Wang P, Luo YF, Jianfeng Huang, Shenghan Gao, Guopeng Zhu, Zhiguo Dang, Jiangtao Gai, Meng Yang, Min Zhu, Huangkai Zhang, Xiuxu Ye, Aiping Gao, Xinyu Tan, Sen Wang, Shuangyang Wu, Edgar B. Cahoon, Beibei Bai, Zhichang Zhao, Qian Li, Junya Wei, Huarui Chen, Ruixiong Luo, Deyong Gong, Kexuan Tang, Bing Zhang, Zhangguang Ni, Guodi Huang, Songnian Hu, Yeyuan Chen: Mango (Mangifera indica) Genome sequencing, assembly, resequencing and RNA sequencing. NCBI Sequence Read Archive, &#xA;https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/bioproject/PRJNA487154&#xA;&#xA; (2020)." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR70" id="ref-link-section-d6606e1991">70</a>]. For additional details about the genome sequencing and de novo assembly, see Additionalfile<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#MOESM1">1</a>: Supplementary Note.</p><h4 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--small" id="Sec15">Genomic assembly quality evaluation</h4><p>To assess the quality of the assembly, we mapped all the pair-end and long reads to the assembly for their mapping rate, which indicates the quality and integrity of the assembly. All the pair-end reads were mapped using BWA-MEM (v0.7.15) [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 79" title="Li H, Durbin R. Fast and accurate short read alignment with Burrows-Wheeler transform. Bioinformatics. 2009;25:175460." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR79" id="ref-link-section-d6606e2004">79</a>], and all the PacBio long reads were mapped using minimap2 [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 80" title="Li H. Minimap2: pairwise alignment for nucleotide sequences. Bioinformatics. 2018;34:3094100." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR80" id="ref-link-section-d6606e2007">80</a>]. the integrity of the protein-coding genes of the assembly was evaluated using Benchmarking Universal Single-copy Orthologs (BUSCO) analysis (v3.0.2, embryophyta_odb9) [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 15" title="Simao FA, Waterhouse RM, Ioannidis P, Kriventseva EV, Zdobnov EM. BUSCO: assessing genome assembly and annotation completeness with single-copy orthologs. Bioinformatics. 2015;31:32102." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR15" id="ref-link-section-d6606e2010">15</a>] and Core Eukaryotic Genes Mapping Approach (CEGMA) analysis (v2.2) [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 14" title="Parra G, Bradnam K, Korf I. CEGMA: a pipeline to accurately annotate core genes in eukaryotic genomes. Bioinformatics. 2007;23:10617." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR14" id="ref-link-section-d6606e2013">14</a>]. Genome completeness was further evaluated by the mapping of 6594 mango genetic markers [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 12" title="Luo C, Shu B, Yao Q, Wu H, Xu W, Wang S. Construction of a high-density genetic map based on large-scale marker development in mango using specific-locus amplified fragment sequencing (SLAF-seq). Front Plant Sci. 2016;7:1310." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR12" id="ref-link-section-d6606e2016">12</a>] and 20,920 Trinity (v 2.2.0) [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 81" title="Haas BJ, Papanicolaou A, Yassour M, Grabherr M, Blood PD, Bowden J, Couger MB, Eccles D, Li B, Lieber M, et al. De novo transcript sequence reconstruction from RNA-seq using the Trinity platform for reference generation and analysis. Nat Protoc. 2013;8:1494512." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR81" id="ref-link-section-d6606e2020">81</a>] assembled transcripts (length&gt;=1kb) from RNA-seq data using BLAT software (v34x10, [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 82" title="Kent WJ. BLAT--the BLAST-like alignment tool. Genome Res. 2002;12:65664." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR82" id="ref-link-section-d6606e2023">82</a>]).</p><h4 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--small" id="Sec16">Genome annotation</h4><p>In prior to gene prediction and annotation, the library of repetitive sequences was ab initio constructed using RepeatModeler. By using this library, repetitive sequences were annotated, classified, and soft-masked by RepeatMasker (<a href="http://www.repeatmasker.org/">http://www.repeatmasker.org/</a>). Transcripts were constructed using a combination of HISAT2 [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 83" title="Kim D, Langmead B, Salzberg SL. HISAT: a fast spliced aligner with low memory requirements. Nat Methods. 2015;12:35760." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR83" id="ref-link-section-d6606e2038">83</a>], Stringtie [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 71" title="Pertea M, Kim D, Pertea GM, Leek JT, Salzberg SL. Transcript-level expression analysis of RNA-seq experiments with HISAT, StringTie and Ballgown. Nat Protoc. 2016;11:165067." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR71" id="ref-link-section-d6606e2041">71</a>], and TACO [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 84" title="Niknafs YS, Pandian B, Iyer HK, Chinnaiyan AM, Iyer MK. TACO produces robust multisample transcriptome assemblies from RNA-seq. Nat Methods. 2017;14:6870." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR84" id="ref-link-section-d6606e2044">84</a>]. The ORFs on the transcripts were extracted using TransDecoder within the PASA pipeline [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 85" title="Haas BJ, Delcher AL, Mount SM, Wortman JR, Smith RK Jr, Hannick LI, Maiti R, Ronning CM, Rusch DB, Town CD, et al. Improving the Arabidopsis genome annotation using maximal transcript alignment assemblies. Nucleic Acids Res. 2003;31:565466." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR85" id="ref-link-section-d6606e2047">85</a>]. The homologous from the Uniprot database (taxonomy: 3398 [Magnoliophyta]) were mapped to the genome using GenomeThreader [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 86" title="Gremme G, Steinbiss S, Kurtz S. GenomeTools: a comprehensive software library for efficient processing of structured genome annotations. IEEE/ACM Trans Comput Biol Bioinform. 2013;10:64556." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR86" id="ref-link-section-d6606e2051">86</a>]. The ab initio prediction of protein-coding gene was carried out by the BRAKER2 pipeline [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 87" title="Hoff KJ, Lomsadze A, Borodovsky M, Stanke M. Whole-genome annotation with BRAKER. Methods Mol Biol. 1962;2019:6595." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR87" id="ref-link-section-d6606e2054">87</a>]. The results from ab initio prediction, homologs, and transcription evidences were integrated using EVM software (v2012-06-25) [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 88" title="Haas BJ, Salzberg SL, Zhu W, Pertea M, Allen JE, Orvis J, White O, Buell CR, Wortman JR. Automated eukaryotic gene structure annotation using EVidenceModeler and the program to assemble spliced alignments. Genome Biol. 2008;9:R7." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR88" id="ref-link-section-d6606e2057">88</a>] and further curated by removing frame-shifts and redundancies using the gffread tool from Cufflinks [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 89" title="Ghosh S, Chan CK. Analysis of RNA-Seq data using TopHat and Cufflinks. Methods Mol Biol. 2016;1374:33961." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR89" id="ref-link-section-d6606e2060">89</a>]. Meanwhile, retro-transposon (RT) genes were identified by HMMER [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 90" title="Eddy SR. Profile hidden Markov models. Bioinformatics. 1998;14:75563." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR90" id="ref-link-section-d6606e2063">90</a>] with the Pfam database and removed from the final annotation. Transcription factor identification was conducted in the plant TF database (<a href="http://planttfdb.cbi.pku.edu.cn/prediction.php">http://planttfdb.cbi.pku.edu.cn/prediction.php</a>) [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 91" title="Jin J, Zhang H, Kong L, Gao G, Luo J. PlantTFDB 3.0: a portal for the functional and evolutionary study of plant transcription factors. Nucleic Acids Res. 2014;42:D11827." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR91" id="ref-link-section-d6606e2071">91</a>]. Non-protein coding genes were detected by the homologous searching of the Rfam database [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 92" title="Griffiths-Jones S, Bateman A, Marshall M, Khanna A, Eddy SR. Rfam: an RNA family database. Nucleic Acids Res. 2003;31:43941." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR92" id="ref-link-section-d6606e2074">92</a>] using Infernal (v1.1.2) [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 93" title="Nawrocki EP, Eddy SR. Infernal 1.1: 100-fold faster RNA homology searches. Bioinformatics. 2013;29:29335." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR93" id="ref-link-section-d6606e2077">93</a>]. Protein annotations were carried out by searching NCBI non-redundant protein database, InterPro [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 94" title="Mulder N, Apweiler R. InterPro and InterProScan: tools for protein sequence classification and comparison. Methods Mol Biol. 2007;396:5970." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR94" id="ref-link-section-d6606e2080">94</a>], and KEGG [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 95" title="Ogata H, Goto S, Sato K, Fujibuchi W, Bono H, Kanehisa M. KEGG: Kyoto Encyclopedia of Genes and Genomes. Nucleic Acids Res. 1999;27:2934." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR95" id="ref-link-section-d6606e2083">95</a>] databases. GO information was extracted from InterPro annotation. For additional details about the genome annotation, see Additionalfile<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#MOESM1">1</a>: Supplementary Notes. The GO enrichment analysis for the retained duplicated genes was performed by GOEAST [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 96" title="Zheng Q, Wang XJ. GOEAST: a web-based software toolkit for Gene Ontology enrichment analysis. Nucleic Acids Res. 2008;36:W35863." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR96" id="ref-link-section-d6606e2090">96</a>] (<a href="http://omicslab.genetics.ac.cn/GOEAST/">http://omicslab.genetics.ac.cn/GOEAST/</a>).</p><h4 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--small" id="Sec17">Comparative genome analysis</h4><p>Twelve species (including mango) representing the major plant domains were selected for phylogenetic analysis. All-versus-all BLASTP [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 97" title="Altschul SF, Gish W, Miller W, Myers EW, Lipman DJ. Basic local alignment search tool. J Mol Biol. 1990;215:40310." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR97" id="ref-link-section-d6606e2105">97</a>] searching results (<i>e</i> value threshold 1e5) were used for gene family construction using OrthoMCL (v2.0.9) [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 98" title="Li L, Stoeckert CJ Jr, Roos DS. OrthoMCL: identification of ortholog groups for eukaryotic genomes. Genome Res. 2003;13:217889." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR98" id="ref-link-section-d6606e2111">98</a>] with series <i>I</i> values. The nucleotide sequences of 248 single-copy genes were concatenated from CDS alignments guided by individual protein alignments using Clustalw2 (v2.1) [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 99" title="Larkin MA, Blackshields G, Brown NP, Chenna R, McGettigan PA, McWilliam H, Valentin F, Wallace IM, Wilm A, Lopez R, et al. Clustal W and Clustal X version 2.0. Bioinformatics. 2007;23:29478." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR99" id="ref-link-section-d6606e2117">99</a>] The best model (HKY+I+G) was selected by Jmodeltest (v2.1.7), and then a ML tree was constructed with 100 bootstrap value using PhyML (v3.1) [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 100" title="Guindon S, Delsuc F, Dufayard JF, Gascuel O. Estimating maximum likelihood phylogenies with PhyML. Methods Mol Biol. 2009;537:11337." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR100" id="ref-link-section-d6606e2121">100</a>]. And the resulting ML tree was used as an input tree for the Caf software and PAML MCMCTree program. The PAML [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 101" title="Yang Z. PAML: a program package for phylogenetic analysis by maximum likelihood. Comput Appl Biosci. 1997;13:5556." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR101" id="ref-link-section-d6606e2124">101</a>] MCMCTree program was used to estimate the species divergence times with the HKY85 model. We used the <i>A. thaliana</i> and <i>C. papaya</i> divergence time (6872 million years ago) [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 18" title="Ming R, Hou S, Feng Y, Yu Q, Dionne-Laporte A, Saw JH, Senin P, Wang W, Ly BV, Lewis KL, et al. The draft genome of the transgenic tropical fruit tree papaya (Carica papaya Linnaeus). Nature. 2008;452:9916." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR18" id="ref-link-section-d6606e2133">18</a>] and the monocot and eudicot divergence time (130240 million years ago) [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 23" title="Jaillon O, Aury JM, Noel B, Policriti A, Clepet C, Casagrande A, Choisne N, Aubourg S, Vitulo N, Jubin C, et al. The grapevine genome sequence suggests ancestral hexaploidization in major angiosperm phyla. Nature. 2007;449:4637." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR23" id="ref-link-section-d6606e2136">23</a>] as calibrators. The MCMC analysis was run for 20,000 generations, using a burn-in of 2000 iterations. Caf software (v3.2, [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 102" title="De Bie T, Cristianini N, Demuth JP, Hahn MW. CAFE: a computational tool for the study of gene family evolution. Bioinformatics. 2006;22:126971." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR102" id="ref-link-section-d6606e2140">102</a>]) was used to identify the gene family that had undergone expansions or contractions for the 2903 gene families with at least 20 members among 12 plant genomes.</p><h4 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--small" id="Sec18">Genome duplication analysis</h4><p>MCScanX [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 103" title="Wang Y, Tang H, Debarry JD, Tan X, Li J, Wang X, Lee TH, Jin H, Marler B, Guo H, et al. MCScanX: a toolkit for detection and evolutionary analysis of gene synteny and collinearity. Nucleic Acids Res. 2012;40:e49." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR103" id="ref-link-section-d6606e2152">103</a>] was used for syntenic region detection with the all-to-all BLASTP results (blocks with at least 10 pairs homologous genes and the gap was less than 5 genes) for orange/mango, orange/longan, mango/longan, and mango/mango. The <i>Ks</i> between the syntenic homologous gene pairs was calculated by PAML (v4.8) [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 101" title="Yang Z. PAML: a program package for phylogenetic analysis by maximum likelihood. Comput Appl Biosci. 1997;13:5556." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR101" id="ref-link-section-d6606e2158">101</a>] using the YN00 NG model.</p><p>For the definition of mango duplicated gene, firstly, the duplicate_gene_classifier module in MCScan software was used to classify the duplicate genes into WGD/segmental duplication (10 homologous gene pairs in collinear blocks), tandem (consecutive repeat), proximal (in nearby genomic region but adjacent within 10 genes), or dispersed (other modes than segmental, tandem and proximal) duplications. The remaining genes were defined as singletons. Secondly, the WGD/segmental duplicated genes were further classified into two subclasses: the gene pairs located in syntenic blocks with the median <i>Ks</i> of 0.30.4 were defined as the genes retained from recent WGD, and the rest were defined as the genes retained from ancient WGD.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec19">Manual revision for certain genes and gene families</h3><p>Anthocyanin, carotenoid, chlorophyll, isoprenoids, lipid, and sugar metabolism-related genes, as well as photosynthesis genes functionally characterized in <i>A. thaliana</i> were retrieved for their corresponding protein sequences from the Arabidopsis Information Resource (TAIR) (<a href="https://www.arabidopsis.org/index.jsp">https://www.arabidopsis.org/index.jsp</a>). The retrieved <i>A. thaliana</i> proteins were processed with InterProScan [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 94" title="Mulder N, Apweiler R. InterPro and InterProScan: tools for protein sequence classification and comparison. Methods Mol Biol. 2007;396:5970." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR94" id="ref-link-section-d6606e2186">94</a>] and BLASTP [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 97" title="Altschul SF, Gish W, Miller W, Myers EW, Lipman DJ. Basic local alignment search tool. J Mol Biol. 1990;215:40310." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR97" id="ref-link-section-d6606e2189">97</a>] (i value=1e10) searched against mango proteins. Hits sharing &gt;30% amino acid identity and &gt;50% amino acid alignment length with the <i>A. thaliana</i> homologs were further checked for Pfam domains. Lipid genes are retrieved from the Arabidopsis Lipid Gene Database [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 104" title="Li-Beisson Y, Shorrosh B, Beisson F, Andersson MX, Arondel V, Bates PD, Baud S, Bird D, Debono A, Durrett TP, et al. Acyl-lipid metabolism. Arabidopsis book. 2013;11:e0161." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR104" id="ref-link-section-d6606e2196">104</a>]. Genes involved in the photosynthesis and sugar metabolism are retrieved based on the information provided in Plant Metabolic Network [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 105" title="Zhang P, Dreher K, Karthikeyan A, Chi A, Pujar A, Caspi R, Karp P, Kirkup V, Latendresse M, Lee C, et al. Creation of a genome-wide metabolic pathway database for Populus trichocarpa using a new approach for reconstruction and curation of metabolic pathways for plants. Plant Physiol. 2010;153:147991." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR105" id="ref-link-section-d6606e2199">105</a>] (<a href="https://www.plantcyc.org">https://www.plantcyc.org</a>). Polyphenol metabolism and chlorophyll metabolism genes were retrieved based on references [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 41" title="Zhu X, Chen J, Qiu K, Kuai B. Phytohormone and light regulation of chlorophyll degradation. Front Plant Sci. 2017;8:1911." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR41" id="ref-link-section-d6606e2206">41</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 106" title="Tohge T, Watanabe M, Hoefgen R, Fernie AR. The evolution of phenylpropanoid metabolism in the green lineage. Crit Rev Biochem Mol Biol. 2013;48:12352." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR106" id="ref-link-section-d6606e2209">106</a>]. Carotenoid biosynthesis genes were retrieved from AtIPD [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 107" title="Vranova E, Hirsch-Hoffmann M, Gruissem W. AtIPD: a curated database of Arabidopsis isoprenoid pathway models and genes for isoprenoid network analysis. Plant Physiol. 2011;156:165560." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR107" id="ref-link-section-d6606e2213">107</a>].</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec20">Population genetics analysis</h3><p>Qualified NGS reads from mango cultivars, landraces, and wild relatives (~20 genomic coverage for each genome) were mapped to the mango genome with Mem module in BWA (v 0.7.15, 79). The raw data of genome resequencing are deposited in the NCBI Sequence Read Archive under project ID PRJNA487154 [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 70" title="Wang P, Luo YF, Jianfeng Huang, Shenghan Gao, Guopeng Zhu, Zhiguo Dang, Jiangtao Gai, Meng Yang, Min Zhu, Huangkai Zhang, Xiuxu Ye, Aiping Gao, Xinyu Tan, Sen Wang, Shuangyang Wu, Edgar B. Cahoon, Beibei Bai, Zhichang Zhao, Qian Li, Junya Wei, Huarui Chen, Ruixiong Luo, Deyong Gong, Kexuan Tang, Bing Zhang, Zhangguang Ni, Guodi Huang, Songnian Hu, Yeyuan Chen: Mango (Mangifera indica) Genome sequencing, assembly, resequencing and RNA sequencing. NCBI Sequence Read Archive, &#xA;https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/bioproject/PRJNA487154&#xA;&#xA; (2020)." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR70" id="ref-link-section-d6606e2225">70</a>]. The alignment for each genome was processed by marking duplicated reads using Picard tools (v 1.119) (<a href="https://github.com/broadinstitute/picard">https://github.com/broadinstitute/picard</a>). The reads in insertion/deletion (Indel) regions were realigned using RealignerTargetCreator and IndelRealigner modules in the Genome Analysis Toolkit (GATK) [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 108" title="McKenna A, Hanna M, Banks E, Sivachenko A, Cibulskis K, Kernytsky A, Garimella K, Altshuler D, Gabriel S, Daly M, DePristo MA. The Genome Analysis Toolkit: a MapReduce framework for analyzing next-generation DNA sequencing data. Genome Res. 2010;20:1297303." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR108" id="ref-link-section-d6606e2232">108</a>]. Variant calling for each genome was carried out by GATK HaplotypeCaller to produce VCF files. All VCFs for 53 genomes were merged to single VCF file by GATK Genotype GVCFs function (v3.5). SNPs were filtered to remove variants with total a depth across genomes of &lt;265 (an average of 5 per genome) and depth &gt;2120 (approximately twice the mean depth of 20 for each genome), these with more than 2 missing genotypes. The gene-based annotation of the resulting qualified variants using ANNOVAR (v3.5c) [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 109" title="Wang K, Li M, Hakonarson H. ANNOVAR: functional annotation of genetic variants from high-throughput sequencing data. Nucleic Acids Res. 2010;38:e164." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR109" id="ref-link-section-d6606e2235">109</a>].</p><p>The fourfold degenerate sites were identified according to the genomic location of gene model [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 110" title="Tang H, Wang X, Bowers JE, Ming R, Alam M, Paterson AH. Unraveling ancient hexaploidy through multiply-aligned angiosperm gene maps. Genome Res. 2008;18:194454." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR110" id="ref-link-section-d6606e2241">110</a>], and 370,924 SNPs located in these sites were identified and used for genetic distance calculation, the principal component analysis, and the population structure analysis. The genetic distance among each combination of 2 genomes was calculated using the equation used in heterozygous human genome [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 111" title="Gronau I, Hubisz MJ, Gulko B, Danko CG, Siepel A. Bayesian inference of ancient human demography from individual genome sequences. Nat Genet. 2011;43:10314." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR111" id="ref-link-section-d6606e2244">111</a>]. A phylogenetic tree was constructed using the neighbor-joining method implemented in PHYLIP (v3.697) [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 112" title="Felsenstein J. PHYLIP - Phylogeny Inference Package (version 3.2). Cladistics. 1989;5:3." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR112" id="ref-link-section-d6606e2247">112</a>] and displayed in Evolview [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 113" title="He Z, Zhang H, Gao S, Lercher MJ, Chen WH, Hu S. Evolview v2: an online visualization and management tool for customized and annotated phylogenetic trees. Nucleic Acids Res. 2016;44:W23641." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR113" id="ref-link-section-d6606e2250">113</a>] (<a href="http://www.evolgenius.info/evolview/">http://www.evolgenius.info/evolview/</a>). The principal component analysis was conducted using EIGENSOFT 4.2 software [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 114" title="Patterson N, Price AL, Reich D. Population structure and eigenanalysis. PLoS Genet. 2006;2:e190." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR114" id="ref-link-section-d6606e2258">114</a>]. Population structure analysis was performed with STRUCTURE [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 115" title="Pritchard JK, Stephens M, Donnelly P. Inference of population structure using multilocus genotype data. Genetics. 2000;155:94559." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR115" id="ref-link-section-d6606e2261">115</a>] using the admixture and no linkage models in a burn-in length of 2000 and 2000 replicates type with 10 replicates. The best <i>k</i> (<i>k</i>=3) was selected by Structure Harvester (v0.6.93) [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 116" title="Earl DA, vonHolt BM. STRUCTURE HARVESTER: a website and program for visualizing STRUCTURE output and implementing the Evanno method. Conserv Genet Resour. 2012;4:3." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR116" id="ref-link-section-d6606e2270">116</a>]. The STRUCTURE results with <i>k</i> values from 2 to 4 were further permuted with program CLUMPP (v1.1.2) [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 117" title="Jakobsson M, Rosenberg NA. CLUMPP: a cluster matching and permutation program for dealing with label switching and multimodality in analysis of population structure. Bioinformatics. 2007;23:18016." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR117" id="ref-link-section-d6606e2277">117</a>] and displayed by the software Distruct (v1.1) [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 118" title="Rosenberg NA. distruct: a program for the graphical display of population structure. Mol Ecol Notes. 2004;4:2." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR118" id="ref-link-section-d6606e2280">118</a>].</p><p>The value of nucleotide diversity ratios (<i></i>) was calculated in 20-kb sliding windows and a step size of 10kb using VariScan (v 2.0.3) [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 119" title="Vilella AJ, Blanco-Garcia A, Hutter S, Rozas J. VariScan: analysis of evolutionary patterns from large-scale DNA sequence polymorphism data. Bioinformatics. 2005;21:27913." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR119" id="ref-link-section-d6606e2289">119</a>] for the populations of <i>Mangifera</i> outgroups, populations of Southeast Asia type (<i>n</i>=16), and India type (<i>n</i>=8) with little or no admixture in the STRUCTURE analysis. VCFtools (v0.1.14, [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 120" title="Danecek P, Auton A, Abecasis G, Albers CA, Banks E, DePristo MA, Handsaker RE, Lunter G, Marth GT, Sherry ST, et al. The variant call format and VCFtools. Bioinformatics. 2011;27:21568." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR120" id="ref-link-section-d6606e2302">120</a>]) were used to calculate per-individual inbreeding coefficients, the regions of runs of homozygosity (ROH), and the pairwise population differentiation levels (<i>F</i><sub>ST</sub>) of three populations (<i>Mangifera</i> outgroups, Southeast Asia type, and India type) with 50-kb sliding window and 20-kb step. Genome-wide high-confident SNPs were used for the calculation of nucleotide diversity ratios (<i></i>) and pairwise population differentiation (<i>F</i><sub>ST</sub>).</p></div></div></section>
                    <section aria-labelledby="availability-of-data-and-materials" data-title="Availability of data and materials"><div class="c-article-section" id="availability-of-data-and-materials-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="availability-of-data-and-materials">Availability of data and materials</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="availability-of-data-and-materials-content">
              
              <p>All raw sequencing reads have been deposited in the NCBI Sequence Read Archive (<a href="https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/sra">https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/sra</a>) under project PRJNA487154 [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 70" title="Wang P, Luo YF, Jianfeng Huang, Shenghan Gao, Guopeng Zhu, Zhiguo Dang, Jiangtao Gai, Meng Yang, Min Zhu, Huangkai Zhang, Xiuxu Ye, Aiping Gao, Xinyu Tan, Sen Wang, Shuangyang Wu, Edgar B. Cahoon, Beibei Bai, Zhichang Zhao, Qian Li, Junya Wei, Huarui Chen, Ruixiong Luo, Deyong Gong, Kexuan Tang, Bing Zhang, Zhangguang Ni, Guodi Huang, Songnian Hu, Yeyuan Chen: Mango (Mangifera indica) Genome sequencing, assembly, resequencing and RNA sequencing. NCBI Sequence Read Archive, &#xA;https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/bioproject/PRJNA487154&#xA;&#xA; (2020)." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-020-01959-8#ref-CR70" id="ref-link-section-d6606e2395">70</a>].</p>

Sivankalyani, N. Sela, O. Feygenberg, H. Zemach, D. Maurer, N. Alkan, " /><meta itemprop="datePublished" content="2016" /><meta itemprop="headline" content="Sivankalyani V, Sela N, Feygenberg O, Zemach H, Maurer D, Alkan N. YC, SH, and PW designed the research. YC, JH, ZN, and GH prepared the research materials. PW, YL, JH, SG, ZD, JG, MY, MZ, HZ, XY, AG, XT, SW, SW, BB, SH, and YC analyzed the data. YC, SH, PW, YL, SG, GZ, ZN, and GH designed and coordinated the genome deep sequencing, assembly, resequencing, annotation, and transcriptomic and comparative genomic analyses. YL, PW, and YC performed the evolutionary analysis. PW, YL, and SG drafted the manuscript. EBC, SH, and YC revised the manuscript. JW, HC, RL, DG, and KT participated in the manuscript preparation. ZZ, QL, and BZ participated in the pant sampling, sequencing, and data analysis. All authors read and approved the final manuscript.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="corresponding-author">Corresponding authors</h3><p id="corresponding-author-list">Correspondence to
